        <p class="date">
         Wed Jan 14, 2015 at 12:48 PM PST
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2015/01/14/1357767/-JP-Morgan-Chase-CEO-Jamie-Dimon-has-a-sad" id="titleHref">
          JP Morgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon has a sad
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/gjohnsit">
          gjohnsit
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=15813&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2015/01/14/1357767/-JP-Morgan-Chase-CEO-Jamie-Dimon-has-a-sad" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="JP Morgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon has a sad" data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2015/01/14/1357767/-JP-Morgan-Chase-CEO-Jamie-Dimon-has-a-sad" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="149" data-story_id="1357767" href="/story/2015/01/14/1357767/-JP-Morgan-Chase-CEO-Jamie-Dimon-has-a-sad#comments">
           149 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <p>
          Why oh why is everyone picking on Jamie these days?
         </p>
         <p>
          Poor little multi-billionaire Jamie Dimon is
          <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2015-01-14/jpmorgan-ceo-dimon-says-banks-under-assault-by-u-s-regulators.html">
           being picked on
          </a>
          by the big, bad government.
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          Jamie Dimon, grappling with multibillion-dollar legal costs and rising capital requirements at JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. (JPM), lashed out at U.S. regulators for
          <b>
           putting his bank under assault.
          </b>
          <br/>
          We have five or six regulators or people coming after us on every different issue, Dimon, 58, said today on a call with reporters after New York-based JPMorgan reported fourth-quarter results.
          <b>
           Its a hard thing to deal with.
          </b>
         </blockquote>
         Poor Jamie. Being a banker is hard these days. After all, Jamie knows that they were
         <a href="http://www.commondreams.org/news/2013/01/23/jp-morgans-jamie-dimon-spurs-outrage-davos">
          "scapegoated"
         </a>
         for the 2008 economic meltdown.
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
         <p>
          So JP Morgan Chase did a little
          <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/wonkblog/wp/2013/10/21/everything-you-need-to-know-about-jpmorgans-13-billion-settlement/">
           mortgage fraud
          </a>
          . Who doesn't, right?
          <br/>
          The important thing is that the
          <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/katrina-vanden-heuvel-jpmorgan-settlement-is-justice-not-a-shakedown/2013/10/29/1eabf704-4015-11e3-a751-f032898f2dbc_story.html">
           shareholders paid the fine
          </a>
          for the crime that he committed, and that's all that matters.
         </p>
         <p>
          And yes, there was the
          <a href="http://www.reuters.com/article/2013/10/21/us-jpmorgan-whale-idUSBRE99K16A20131021">
           London Whale scandal
          </a>
          , but what's a few billion between friends?
         </p>
         <p>
          And yes, they
          <a href="http://www.usatoday.com/story/money/business/2013/07/30/jpmorgan-power-manipulation-ferc/2598861/">
           rigged energy prices
          </a>
          in California and midwest.
         </p>
         <p>
          And of course, there was
          <a href="http://dealbook.nytimes.com/2013/03/03/banks-find-more-wrongful-foreclosures-among-military-members/?_r=0">
           wrongful foreclosures
          </a>
          on military members, and
          <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2011/POLITICS/02/10/congress.military.mortgages/">
           overcharging on military home loans
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          $100 million to settle charges of
          <a href="http://www.reuters.com/article/2012/07/24/us-jpmorgan-creditcard-settlement-idUSBRE86N13O20120724">
           bilking credit card holders
          </a>
          with improper fees and interest rates
         </p>
         <p>
          $1.2 Billion to settle charges of
          <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2012-08-09/jpmorgan-says-credit-card-swipe-case-cost-1-2-billion.html">
           conspiring with Visa and MasterCard
          </a>
          to rig swipe fees
         </p>
         <p>
          $228 million to settle charges of
          <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/business/economy/jp-morgan-charged-with-rigging-municipal-bond-deals/2011/07/07/gIQAlRQA2H_story.html">
           rigging the municipal bond market
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Involvement in
          <a href="http://www.lexology.com/library/detail.aspx?g=84290dbe-5ad8-4aec-91ca-3de525b86914">
           manipulating the EURIBOR
          </a>
          interest rates.
         </p>
         <p>
          Involvement in
          <a href="http://www.businessweek.com/news/2013-11-01/barclays-citigroup-among-banks-sued-over-wm-reuters-rates-1">
           manipulating WM/Reuter
          </a>
          interest rates
         </p>
         <p>
          Involvement in
          <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/08/09/jpmorgan-chase-libor-subpoenas_n_1760015.html">
           manipulating he LIBOR
          </a>
          interest rates, as well as a
          <a href="http://www.ftadviser.com/2013/11/06/regulation/regulators/libor-banks-face-court-action-in-new-york-ytyezFJw6qrKEZB0nYFa8N/article.html">
           separate lawsuit
          </a>
          involving the LIBOR
         </p>
         <p>
          But that was
          <i>
           last
          </i>
          year. It's 2015 now.
          <br/>
          Last week JP Morgan agreed to
          <a href="http://www.reuters.com/article/2015/01/05/us-jpmorgan-forex-jpmorgan-idUSKBN0KE1A420150105">
           pay another $1 Billion in fines
          </a>
          for rigging the currency markets.
         </p>
         <p>
          So we should let bygones be bygones.
         </p>
         <p>
          The take-away from all this is that government regulators are
          <i>
           clearly
          </i>
          over-reacting.
         </p>
         <p>
          Just because JP Morgan Chase is running its business like a criminal syndicate doesn't mean that the government should be sticking its nose in the free market, amirite?
          <br/>
         </p>
         <div class="dkimg-c">
          <span class="image_container">
           <img alt="" height="483" src="http://images.dailykos.com/images/124364/large/criminal_syndicate.jpg?1421268105" width="500"/>
          </span>
         </div>
         But will anyone listen to the lamentations of Jamie Dimon?
         <blockquote>
          In the old days, you dealt with one regulator when you had an issue, maybe two, said Dimon, 58. Now its five or six. It makes it very difficult and very complicated. You all should ask the question about
          <b>
           how American that is. And how fair that is
          </b>
          . And how complex that is for companies.
         </blockquote>
         Yes, in the "old days" when financial regulators weren't do their jobs and bankers could commit crimes willy-nilly...Yes, those were the days.
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tags">

         Tags

        <style>

        <br/>
        <div>
         <p>
          Add keywords that describe this diary.
		Separate multiple keywords with commas.
          <br/>
          <a href="/special/tag_tips" target="_blank">
           Tagging tips
          </a>
          -
          <a href="/search?search_tags=1" target="_blank">
           Search For Tags
          </a>
          -
          <a href="http://www.dkosopedia.com/wiki/Tag:Tagfinder" target="_blank">
           Browse For Tags
          </a>
         </p>
         <div class="pageTip hasTooltip" style="margin-top:3px">
          ?
         </div>
         <div class="tooltipContents qtip-style-dk4_large qtip-pos-br">
          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>
         </div>
         <!-- &lt;h4 id="p_tagErrorMessage"&gt;You must enter at least one Tag for this Diary Entry:&lt;/h4&gt; -->
         <p>
          <input id="p_tagInput" name="tag_draft" size="70" type="text" value=""/>
          <!-- &lt;input id="tagSubmit" type="submit" name="submit" value="Submit" /&gt; -->
         </p>
         <p style="font-style:italic">
          Consider if one or more of these tags fits your diary:
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Civil Rights');return false;">
           Civil Rights
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Community');return false;">
           Community
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Congress');return false;">
           Congress
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Culture');return false;">
           Culture
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Economy');return false;">
           Economy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Education');return false;">
           Education
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Elections');return false;">
           Elections
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Energy');return false;">
           Energy
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Environment');return false;">
           Environment
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Health Care');return false;">
           Health Care
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('International');return false;">
           International
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Labor');return false;">
           Labor
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Law');return false;">
           Law
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Media');return false;">
           Media
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Meta');return false;">
           Meta
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('National Security');return false;">
           National Security
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Science');return false;">
           Science
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Transportation');return false;">
           Transportation
          </a>
          , or
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('White House');return false;">
           White House
          </a>
          .
	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('California');return false;">
           California
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="#" onclick="addTagToField('Texas');return false;">
           Texas
          </a>
          , etc).
	Keep in mind, though, that there are many wonderful and important diaries
	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.
         </p>

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               in 1974 I was remodeling the 50 year old Mar Monte Hotel in Santa Barbara California. For few Days I was on a crew yanking out the old windows. We made a minimum of cuts and using hammers and 3 foot crow bars to force them out with prejudice .one window sprang lose easier then the others and the sash weight swung out on the cord like the end of a bull whip and hit Bruno Winkler in the nut sack. He went down like a Idaho Senator. We laughed a lot, except Bruno. The next day he said his scrote was black and blue, but we didn't want , have or get to see it. True dat

           <li id="c130">
            <div class="cx" id="cx55427794">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               Two Problems
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1357767/55427794#c130?mode=alone;showrate=1#c130">
                0+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               First, wishing ill on someone without having the will to perform the deed yourself is a shade of cowardice.
              </p>
              <p>
               Second, Wei Wu Wei does not mean what you think it means. It's not "Not-doing is doing," it's "Doing not-doing," and that does not mean that doing nothing is still a choice, or a decision. That phrase is meant to be paired with the axiom, "The way that can be taught, is not The Eternal Way."
              </p>
              <p>
               That axiom is meant to work no matter what kind of subject-verb combos you throw into it. "The way that can be weighed is not The Eternal Way," The name that can be named is not The Eternal Name," and last and perhaps most importantly, the force that can be forced is not The Eternal Force." This could just as easily be re-framed to "The action that can be performed is not The Eternal Action," in reference to Wei Wu Wei. Wei Wu Wei is a state of mind/being, when you get out of your own way. Some people like to describe this as "in the zone." Other people call it "the artist's release."
              </p>
              <p>
               This can be simply described as an action so completely natural that it moves the actor, rather than the actor making a move. To accomplish "not-doing," requires that one stop trying and allow the action to come naturally. Zen Buddhists have a word to describe a similar experience; Satori.
              </p>
              <p>
               Wei Wu Wei is not a fancy means of saying "Deciding to not act is still making a choice, to allow something to happen is still an action of some kind," or more clearly, "Evil prospers when good people do nothing."
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
              </p>
              <p class="cb">
               by
               <a href="/user/uid:1018882">
                Tyshalle
               </a>
               on
               <a href="/comments/1357767/55427794#c130">
                Thu Jan 15, 2015 at 04:22:43 PM PST
               </a>
              </p>
              <p class="cl">
               [
               <a href="#c58">
                Parent
               </a>
               ]
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </ul>

               <a href="/user/uid:1003349">
                silverfoxcruiser
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              Wachovia was pretty good at
              <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/world/2011/apr/03/us-bank-mexico-drug-gangs">
               laundering money for drug gangs
              </a>
              , but they went out of business, and
              <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2013-07-02/hsbc-judge-approves-1-9b-drug-money-laundering-accord.html">
               HSBC
              </a>
              took over that market, along with the terrorist organization market.
             </p>
            </div>

               </a>
               <span class="cu">
                I remember the years before Wachovia took over
               </span>
               <span class="crd ntb">
                (
                <a href="/comments/1357767/55429660#c135?mode=alone;showrate=1#c135">
                 1+ / 0-
                </a>

               </span>

              <div class="crs">

                </dt>
                <dd>
                 <a href="/user/uid:23833">
                  Dburn
                 </a>

               </dl>
              </div>
              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                the previous bank which was owned by a couple in a nearby town, who were trusted by all customers (they were very highly regarded and the bank did well until they decided to retire) I'd had my personal account there for some time.
               </p>
               <p>
                I left my account there as it was easier than trying to figure out where else to take it. My husband's personal account and a property account were at Wells Fargo.
               </p>
               <p>
                Then Wells Fargo took over Wachovia. At that point, I figured the nearest bank of any brand was Wells Fargo, so I've had my account there ever since. It's only 3 blocks to the ATM, quite handy. I must say the people working there are always very helpful if I have any questions, though the faces change frequently!
               </p>
              </div>

             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              Wachovia's fine
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              From
              <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/world/2011/apr/03/us-bank-mexico-drug-gangs">
               this link
              </a>
             </p>
             <blockquote>
              Now that the year's "deferred prosecution" has expired, the bank is in effect in the clear. It paid federal authorities $110m in forfeiture, for allowing transactions later proved to be connected to drug smuggling, and incurred a $50m fine for failing to monitor cash used to ship 22 tons of cocaine.
              <br/>
              More shocking, and more important, the bank was sanctioned for failing to apply the proper anti-laundering strictures to the transfer of $378.4bn  a sum equivalent to one-third of Mexico's gross national product  into dollar accounts from so-called casas de cambio (CDCs) in Mexico, currency exchange houses with which the bank did business.
              <br/>
              "Wachovia's blatant disregard for our banking laws gave international cocaine cartels a virtual carte blanche to finance their operations," said Jeffrey Sloman, the federal prosecutor. Yet the total fine was less than 2% of the bank's $12.3bn profit for 2009.
             </blockquote>
             A $110
             <i>
              million
             </i>
             fine on $378.4
             <b>
              billion
             </b>
             is FAR less than the profits Wachovia made on the money laudering.
            </div>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             in total assets, and probably many times that in exposure. That's one regulator for every $353,000,000.00 That hardly seems like over-regulation to me.
            </p>
            <p>
             I think that the big banks should be assessed a special tax to provide real oversight. A bank of this size should have hundreds of regulators and government auditors, not 5 or 6, and they should be truly independent and not embedded and subject to "regulatory capture" by the industry.
            </p>
            <p>
             F*ck 'em. Truly. What are they going to do, go out of business? This is North America. There will always be banks and banking and lots of money to be made, and it's not too much to ask that they make money
             <em>
              legally
             </em>
             . The government has every right and every obligation to regulate these banks, prosecute violations, and jail offenders.

              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:78397">
               CA Nana
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:19024">
               joynow
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:167631">
               Egalitare
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:1135154">
               meagsp
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             ... if you think about what $1 billion can do to save or improve lives, one starts to think about appropriate penalties for these sorts of crimes.
            </p>
            <p>
             These guys almost never end up being held criminally liable for what they do. Rigging municipal bonds or commodities markets or exchange rates
             <em>
              to the tune of billions
             </em>
             ultimately causes deaths. It distorts and diverts resources that could be spent in other ways, or that assure people's ability to make a living and support their families, or results in additional burdens spread widely among millions. The cumulative effect is huge, worse than murder, even if the harm to each individual is small. Manipulating hundreds of thousands of mortgages? Did this contribute to any suicides?
            </p>
            <p>
             What penalty is appropriate for a financial crime of such magnitude? Seems to me that life imprisonment without parole is completely appropriate.
            </p>
           </div>

           <p>
            The opening of "Rich Boy" (1925):
            <br/>
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            Let me tell you about the very rich. They are different from you and me. They possess and enjoy early, and it does something to them, makes them soft where we are hard, and cynical where we are trustful, in a way that, unless you were born rich, it is very difficult to understand. They think, deep in their hearts, that they are better than we are because we had to discover the compensations and refuges of life for ourselves. Even when they enter deep into our world or sink below us, they still think that they are better than we are. They are different.
           </blockquote>

            <p>
             Larry Summers: Goldman Sacked
             <br/>
             Greg Palast | Investigative Reporter
             <br/>

             If you want to know why Obama would choose such a grifter and gamer to head the Fed, you have to ask, Who picked Obama? Ten years ago, Barry Obama was a nothing, a State Senator from the South Side of Chicago.
             <p>
              But then, he got lucky. A local bank, Superior, was shut down by regulators for mortgage shenanigans ripping off Black folk. The bank's Chairwoman,
              <strong>
               Penny Pritzker
              </strong>
              was so angry at regulators, she decided to eliminate them: and that required a new President.
             </p>
             <p>
              The billionaires connected Obama to
              <strong>
               Jamie Dimon
              </strong>
              of J.P. Morgan, but most importantly to
              <strong>
               Robert Rubin
              </strong>
              , former Treasury Secretary, but most important, former CEO of Goldman Sachs and mentor of
              <strong>
               Larry Summers
              </strong>
              .
              <strong>
               <em>
                Without Rubin's blessing and overwhelming fundraising power, Obama would still be arguing over zoning on Halsted Street.
               </em>
              </strong>
             </p>
             <p>
              <strong>
               <em>
                Rubin picked Obama and Obama picks whom Rubin picks for him.
               </em>
              </strong>
             </p>
             <p>
              Because, in the end, Obama knows he must choose a Fed chief based on the answer to one question: What would Goldman think?
             </p>

  <script type="text/javascript">
   if($.cookie('meter_user') !== 'false') {
		if ($('#ePostButton').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('#ePostButton').click(function() { 
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Posted Comment', { 
		      repliedTo: $(this).parents('#eP').prevAll('.cb').children('a').first().html() 
		    });
		  });
		}
		
		if (!!document.location.pathname.match('activate') &amp;&amp; $('h1:contains("Welcome to Daily Kos!")').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Signed Up');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname === '/') {
		  if (document.location.hostname.match(/^www|^dailykos/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Front Page');
		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
